## **130: The Theocracy and a Detour**

**AN:** It’s possible that I might change Sakura’s surname someday.

…I thought it was fine since it’s an old classic, but then they go and release a sequel.

---

Two days after taming the mermaid, we finally finished our long journey through the forest.

That said, there really wasn’t anything worth talking about during those two days.

Territorially, we were still within the Kingdom of Sanokia, but at this pace we would enter the Elgant Theocracy in less than an hour.

After entering the Elgant Theocracy, we would need to pass through about five cities, but by carriage it should take roughly a week to reach the Divine Capital (the capital city).

In the Elgant Theocracy, the roads are well maintained, and if you are heading toward a major city within the country, you can always travel on roads that are paved to some extent. What’s more, there are no detours, and the roads run almost in straight lines.

In fact, there is a historical background to this road paving.

No, it would be more accurate to say there is a Hero-related background to it… Yes, the cultural invasion brought about by Heroes.

The Elgant Theocracy worships the Goddess and provides extensive support to Heroes, who are also apostles of the Goddess, so Heroes visit frequently. In other words, the country is more susceptible to the effects of cultural invasion than others.

“Just worshipping the Goddess already makes it a pain, and hearing that Heroes caused all sorts of trouble makes my legs feel heavy.”

“There are parts of it that help us too, though…”

“Yeah, I can’t deny that either.”

As Sakura said, the various things Heroes have done sometimes end up helping us.

Basically, when Heroes do things, it’s because they want to bring the world closer, even a little, to the civilization they know. Naturally, those of us who lived in the same era find it easier to adapt.

“But it strays far from normal civilizational development.”

Mio’s argument is correct.

The cultural invasion by Heroes must have greatly distorted the civilization this world was originally meant to follow.

“No matter how you look at it, it’s already far too late.”

“Yeah, at this point it’s been messed up so badly that worrying about small things now just feels stupid.”

To be blunt, civilization is already distorted beyond saving.

“Mio, you’ve been advancing civilization in the culinary field too, haven’t you?”

“I make a point not to spread recipes outside my subordinates. The things I put out publicly are dishes that are already known elsewhere, just with some tweaks…”

It seems Mio is at least mindful of cultural invasion.

“Mayo-“

“T-That was a failure, so it doesn’t count!”

Mio hurriedly makes excuses.

“Let me finish what I was saying.”

“No!”

I guess this is just another template scene…

“There are a lot of foods in this world that originated with Heroes.”

“The dishes spread by Heroes are tasty and have a good story behind them, so I think they spread easily.”

“Yes, just as Maria-chan says, most shops advertise that the dish was spread by a Hero. Apparently, sales differ quite a bit.”

If Sera, who is well versed in the state of eateries in this world, says so, then it must be true.

It’s very Japanese, in a sense, but summoned Heroes probably can’t endure a low level of food culture.

That said, it’s not like Japanese food is overflowing everywhere, likely because many summoned Heroes are students. Few Heroes would be able to cook for themselves.

Me? I never planned on cooking for myself from the start. Ingredients are a waste, aren’t they?

“Lately, my favorite has been the three-item set of okonomiyaki, takoyaki, and yakisoba that I ate at Akindo in the Izumo Wa Kingdom. It was proposed by a Hero and is apparently popular with young people.”

“Ah, the three flour-based dishes you were eating when we went together… They’d fill you up, so I can see why young people like them, but the nutritional balance is completely thrown out the window…”

Hearing about Sera’s favorite, Mio stares off into the distance.

It’s a brutal set where everything is carb-heavy and all of it qualifies as a staple food.

《Yakisoba bread was yummy!》

“Do the people of Akindo like stacking staple foods or something?”

Dora seems to have liked yakisoba bread.

It’s a staple plus a staple combo.

Thinking about Dora’s growth at such a young age, I’d like to limit meals with poor nutritional balance.

That said, back in my original world, I half-jokingly made something called sobameshi bread, which combined staple + staple + staple, so I can’t really complain.

By the way, sobameshi was the kind you just microwave. Yakisoba is such an advanced dish that there’s no way I could make it.

“Basically, there are a lot of people who really live by the phrase ‘time is money’, so dishes that fill you up quickly tend to become popular.”

“I see. So that’s the background.”

Meal times can be a surprisingly significant burden.

Unless you really like eating, that is.

…If I made cup noodles, wouldn’t they sell in Akindo?

A: It’s a different country, but a past Hero has already made something similar.

There was one! And they actually managed to make cup noodles!

They really do whatever they want… Cup noodles are a pretty modern cultural product. At least stick to preserved foods like canned goods.

Anyway, that was a bit of a tangent, but to begin with, I don’t think cultural invasion by Heroes is a bad thing.

Because if you summon a Hero, it’s only natural that the civilization the Hero brings with them will spread.

You’re forcibly summoned to another world and made to endure a low standard of living. Then, because you can’t endure it, you bring in the civilization of your homeland. What’s wrong with that?

The ones who chose to summon Heroes were the inhabitants of this world, so they have to be prepared for their world to be invaded by Hero culture. In other words, it’s their own fault.

After chatting like that for an hour.

We finally left the Kingdom of Sanokia and arrived at the border with the Elgant Theocracy.

There was an impressive gate at the border, and our carriage was stopped in front of it.

It seems the Minister of Foreign Affairs is currently in the middle of negotiations with the gate guards. There’s no need for Sakuya to step in just to talk with gate guards, and there’s no need for me to go either. I don’t want to go out.

Well, even if I did go out, I’d probably only be useful for intimidation.

That’s worse than I expected…

After a while, one of the maids came over to our carriage.

“Queen Sakuya, the gate soldiers are requesting to accompany us to the Divine Capital as guides. What shall we do? Also, they have apparently sent out fast riders as advance notice.”

“Advance notice is fine, but guides, huh… Hmm, what should we do? We have maps and even my Special Power’s map, so we know the way, but refusing might seem unnatural. Still, I don’t want to bring along unnecessary people and reveal our hand… More than anything, I don’t want anyone who doesn’t know the situation getting close to my brother…”

Hearing the maid’s report, Sakuya falls into thought.

We’d gone to the trouble of surrounding me with people who know my situation, so letting unnecessary people get close and causing trouble would be unbearable.

“Sakuya, take a look at the map.”

“Ah… This is no good. We can’t take them. Sorry, but please refuse the guides.”

“Understood.”

When I prompted her to check the map, Sakuya immediately refused the guides.

After the maid left, Sakuya muttered with a displeased expression.

“All of them being bright red, seriously…?”

Yes, all of the soldiers of the Elgant Theocracy shown on our map are marked in red, meaning ‘hostile’.

What’s more, most of the residents of the towns and villages within the four visible map areas are also marked red.

“They worship the Goddess and revere Heroes. It’s not strange for them to hold hostility toward me, who killed a Hero.”

“This is already enemy territory. For Lord Jin’s sake, we must remain vigilant.”

“Seems so. I might have underestimated things a bit…”

Maria is, naturally, in a state of heightened alert.

Unfortunately, Maria still hasn’t acquired any precognition-type skills (they’re not something you can get that easily). Given examples like Orihara’s surprise attack, she’s on edge.

“We’ll have to think carefully about stopping by towns.”

《We can’t sightsee? Master, is that okay?》

“Jin-kun, you wouldn’t seriously suggest sightseeing in this situation, right…?”

Sakura asks a bit anxiously.

She probably thinks I might prioritize sightseeing even in this situation.

“Even I wouldn’t want to sightsee when hostility is this blatant. There’s no way it would be enjoyable.”

“That’s true…”

“At the very least, it’ll have to wait until after we reach the Divine Capital once and can act while hiding our identities.”

At the very least, we can’t sightsee while acting as Sakuya’s guards.

It would be best to just set up ‘Portal’ points and leave sightseeing for another time.

“But we can’t just avoid stopping by towns altogether. We might be fine, but the ministers are at their limit. We need to stop by at least one town to let them rest.”

As Sakuya says, the ministers are clearly exhausted.

We’ve pushed them pretty hard, so stopping by a town is essential to let them rest.

“That can’t be helped. For now, let’s stop by the nearest town from here. What happens after that will depend on how that town treats us.”

“I don’t think they’d attack guests invited by the country, but not knowing what they might do is unsettling.”

Sera said that, but would residents of a theocracy really be that rational?

To be honest, I think there’s a chance they might attack us.

“Yeah. They might mess with the food or pull petty harassment. Anyone who does that, Mio-chan doesn’t acknowledge as a cook, though.”

“I will not forgive anyone who harms Lord Jin.”

Maria is as extreme as ever, but with this many enemies, it’s a natural response.

I’m generally not merciful to enemies either.

“That too will depend on the first town. We’ll decide our basic policy toward this country based on that.”

“Yes. As Lord Jin commands.”

And so, our entire approach to this country ended up depending on the first town.

I don’t really like judging a whole country based on one town, but with such a high chance of unpleasant experiences, I have no intention of repeating the experiment multiple times.

About two hours after passing through the border gate.

The name of the first town in the Elgant Theocracy is the town of Elrim.

According to Alta, it’s customary for countries or towns that worship the Goddess to start their names with “El.” The Kingdom of Eldia and the Elgant Theocracy are examples.

Thinking about it that way, maybe naming the Primordial Divine Dragon “El” was a mistake.

L: That’s so mean!

By the way, since they haven’t had any screen time until now, I never had a chance to explain this, but the Primordial Divine Dragon and the Great Spirit are also accompanying us on this journey.

More precisely, it’s not ‘accompanying’ but ‘assimilated’, though…

Since El is a pseudo-personality and is absorbed into me, calling it assimilation is fine.

Rain is the tricky one to explain.

Rain is also a contracted spirit and wanted to accompany me on the journey (in reality, through gestures), but taking a Great Spirit like Rain around as-is would draw too much attention.

Spirits can be stored inside ‘Spirit Luminous Stones’, so we considered taking her along in that state, but the ‘Spirit Luminous Stone’ that houses Rain is extra large and bulky.

So, following Alta’s instructions, we tried absorbing the ‘Spirit Luminous Stone’ using \<Life and Death Authority> strengthened through \<Expanded Interpretation>. By doing so, I inherited part of the properties of the ‘Spirit Luminous Stone’ and became able to retain Rain within myself.

If that explanation doesn’t make much sense, just think of it as a different kind of fusion than ‘Spiritification.’ To be honest, I don’t really understand the logic myself.

Rain seems pleased to be able to always be with me, and except when she’s fine-tuning mana flows in the Brown Wall Kingdom (in other words, working), she prefers to remain assimilated with me at all times.

On the other hand, El would prefer to manifest outside normally, but seems to think it’s dangerous to be away from me when heading to places where anything might happen.

That’s the official reason, but I suspect she’s actually worried that Rain being able to assimilate with me threatens her familiar position. Overlapping roles are scary, right?

Rain doesn’t care about anything else as long as she can be with me, and El is fine as long as her role isn’t stolen by Rain, so we probably won’t have any reason to call either of them out during this journey.

Calling either of them out would mean a serious emergency.

Anyway, back to the main topic.

Now then, after that long detour, let me explain about the town of Elrim.

This town is a major transportation hub between the Elgant Theocracy and the Kingdom of Sanokia, and it’s quite large.

Many traveling merchants come and go, so it’s lively. Normally, when a town grows large, slums tend to form, but this town is known for having an unusually low crime rate, apparently because it puts effort into maintaining public order at the town level.

There are many devout followers of the Goddess religion, and it’s an unspoken rule among merchants not to say anything unnecessary regarding religion.

That’s because when it comes to matters involving the Goddess religion, the town’s good public order does not apply.

Our carriage reached the town of Elrim… and passed right by without stopping.

“That’s a no-go.”

“Yeah, there’s no way. I feel bad for the ministers, but…”

“But I think it’s better than taking them into that town…”

After my verdict, Sakuya and Sakura follow up.

The others seem to agree as well, and no one voices opposition.

The reason we didn’t go into the town can be summed up in one sentence: “They’re coming to kill us.”

Now then, let me explain the events that would occur in the town of Elrim, as revealed by the map.

First, let’s assume we arrive in the town of Elrim.

Since advance notice has been sent, a guide would lead us to inns, but due to poor communication, there wouldn’t be enough rooms for everyone. As a result, we’d be asked to split up and stay between the highest-class inn where Sakuya would stay and another inn that’s slightly lower in rank but still fairly high-class.

Yes. Our forces would be divided here.

Next comes the meal.

The food served at the highest-class inn. Yes, of course, it’s poisoned.

It’s a slow-acting poison that won’t kill you, but it has various adverse effects and will definitely ruin the rest of your life.

In case the poison is discovered before being eaten, a culprit has already been prepared.

The head chef is designated as the culprit, but in reality, that person cannot cook at all.

They exist solely to take the blame. In truth, they’re a detained criminal, and the plan is for them to be dead by the time they’re handed over to us. Even if they can’t cook a single dish, if everyone around them says “he’s the head chef”, then it becomes the truth.

Let’s say we go out into the town.

The townspeople will do everything they can to prevent our scattered forces from regrouping.

Then, pretending it’s an accident, they’ll come to kill us. The frequency isn’t high, but there are instant-death traps set up throughout the town.

The administrators of the locations where the traps are set have already agreed to take responsibility and die if any of us are harmed.

Let’s say we rest at the inn.

Assassins with \<Assassination Arts> are hiding inside the rooms. If we go to sleep, the assassin hiding under the bed will stab us. Multiple assassins are also hiding in the ceiling, and they’ll attack at any opportunity.

As you can see, the town of Elrim is fully prepared to kill us, even if it means taking responsibility and dying… Yes, it’s extremely annoying.

Naturally, the lord is aware of all this. In fact, it was the lord who, after hearing the advance notice, gave the actual orders. That also establishes a pattern of lord = noble-related trouble.

Now then, a question.

Would you want to stop by a town where you know all this will happen?

I absolutely do not.

“Sera, didn’t you say they wouldn’t attack guests invited by the country?”

“This is beyond my expectations. No one would imagine an entire town trying to kill them.”

In some ways it was expected, but the whole town being involved was unexpected.

“Yeah… I don’t think we can expect much from the next town either…”

At this rate, it’s obvious that advance soldiers have already been sent to the next town as well, and the same situation as in Elrim will occur.

Should we just go nonstop to the Divine Capital…?

But we have the ministers with us. I want to let them rest somewhere.

“We could deviate from the route and go to another town, or just bite the bullet and teach them about ‘Portal’ …”

For ministers who already understand a lot, teaching them about ‘Portal’ wouldn’t cause too much harm.

“We still have plenty of time, and I don’t think it’d be a problem to deviate a bit. For the ministers sake, I’d like to enter a town that advance notice hasn’t passed through. I want to avoid spreading information about your abilities as much as possible…”

Sakuya seems to prefer taking a detour rather than using my abilities.

Thanks to cutting straight through the forest in the Kingdom of Sanokia, we have plenty of time, so a detour wouldn’t be an issue. It might be best to avoid unnecessary actions.

“Let’s have Alta pick a relatively safe town.”

“Yeah, please do, big brother.”

“Alright. If things go well, we can even do some sightseeing.”

If we act while hiding our identities, I can sightsee without any reservations.

“In the end, Master always comes back to that…”

“Well, that’s just how it is.”

“As always…”

“Big brother really does love sightseeing.”

For some reason, everyone looks exasperated (except Maria and Dora). I don’t get it.

“Vega, please search for a safe town.”

“Understood.”

Following Alta’s (Vega’s) instructions, we changed direction from our planned route, and after three hours, a relatively safe first town finally came into view.

“Using Alta’s route really does make for quite a detour. Good thing we made the schedule with plenty of leeway…”

After checking the route on the map, Sakuya lets out a sigh of relief.

It seems she’d planned with plenty of time to spare in case anything happened.

With about seventeen days of leeway left before the summit, and considering that going straight to the Divine Capital would take about a week, the plan had been to stay in the Divine Capital for around ten days.

Using Alta’s route adds about three extra days.

It can’t be helped that safe routes take longer (let’s avert our eyes from the forest shortcut).

It’d be cruel to push the ministers any further…

“When we get to town, we’ll pretend to be incognito nobles, right?”

“Yeah. We won’t give names and will pretend to be well-paying nobles. We discussed it with the ministers, so I don’t think there’ll be any issues. I plan to disguise myself a bit too.”

“Sakuya-chan’s kimono really stands out, so changing clothes is essential…”

Since Sakuya’s face might be known, and she can’t walk around in a kimono, she’ll change clothes and disguise herself.

“I’ll disguise myself too, just in case.”

《If Master does it, Dora will too!》

In my case, it’s for sightseeing.

Dora just wants to imitate me.

We stop the carriage and begin preparations to enter the town.

Sakuya ties her long hair into twin tails and changes from a kimono into Western-style clothes.

That alone changes her impression considerably.

I take off my armor and put on ordinary clothes. I put on fake glasses to disguise myself… or at least I think I do.

Dora puts on fake glasses as well.

There’s no way I have the courage to walk around town wearing the ‘Mysterious Noble Mask (concealment item).’

When I come out of the carriage after changing, the ministers give me awkward looks.

“What’s wrong?”

“No… Are you no longer trying to hide your identity?”

When I ask, Finance Minister Rudolf poses the question.

I see. They must be confused because I’d gone to such lengths to hide my identity, only to reveal it so casually here.

“You’d already noticed anyway, right?”

“Yes, well…”

His response is hesitant, but he doesn’t deny it.

“Then there’s no problem. Appearances and formalities matter, but not with insiders. In public, I’ll act as Queen Knight Gene. As long as you understand that, it’s fine.”

“…Understood. We shall treat you accordingly from now on.”

“Yeah, do that.”

Alright, now I don’t need to wear armor inside the carriage anymore.

Mimi’s armor fits well, so it’s not too burdensome, but wearing armor at all is a burden, so there’s no reason to wear it when it doesn’t matter.

We move the carriage again, and finally arrive at the first town of the Elgant Theocracy. The town of Elrim has been completly forgotten.

The town’s name is Elvalley.

It’s not as large as Elrim, but just having lower killing intent already makes it better.

Even so, there’s still a lot of red on the map… If you don’t notice it, you’re safe.

After passing through the gate and securing a high-class inn, the ministers seem to have hit their limit and decided to rest for the day.

Sakuya also decided to stay at the inn, saying she couldn’t go out carelessly. She seems to want to go out, but the ministers strongly opposed it, so she reluctantly agreed.

They’d prefer me to stay behind as a guard as well, but they didn’t press the issue.

We’ve left most of the maid knights at the inn, so I hope that’s enough.

So, leaving Sakuya, Vega, the maid knights, maids, and ministers at the inn, the usual six of us head out into the town of Elvalley.

“There are a lot of white, holy-looking buildings. I guess it lives up to calling itself a divine kingdom.”

Most of the buildings in town are based on white, so the town as a whole feels harmonious.

Many people are also dressed in white, so wherever you look, white inevitably catches your eye.

I don’t dislike towns with a sense of unity. As a tourist destination, at least.

“White is said to be the most revered color in the Goddess religion. It’s also said that the Goddess herself wears white garments. Whether that’s true or not, I don’t know.”

According to Sera, there are many artworks depicting the Goddess, but her hair and eye colors vary.

Idol worship isn’t prohibited, but there are no descriptions of the Goddess’s appearance in Goddess religion materials. However, the color of her clothing is clearly stated as white, so that alone ended up being emphasized.

“So there was a Goddess-related reason, not just the simple idea that white is holy.”

No wonder there’s so much white.

“It looks nice, and Mio-chan actually likes this kind of thing. Sigh… I wish we could’ve come when we weren’t hostile. Also, this town’s food is pretty skewed.”

It was almost dusk, so the town was a bit busy as we walked around, but many of the stalls (painted white) were selling familiar dishes.

As you can probably guess, they were various Japanese dishes left behind by Heroes.

“Croquettes, nikujaga, croquettes, potato salad, croquettes, hashed potatoes, croquettes… What is this all-out potato, croquette push…?”

They’re really pushing potatoes hard.

I don’t dislike potatoes, and there are plenty of dishes I like, but isn’t this a bit much?

“Hey, mister. Why does this town have so many potato dishes? Also, six croquettes, please.”

Curious about the abundance of potato dishes, Mio asks the middle-aged man frying croquettes at the stall. Apparently, this stall’s croquettes smelled the best.

“Hm? Miss, are you from out of town?”

“Yeah, we are.”

“Then it’s no surprise you don’t know.”

As he puts the croquettes into wrapping, the man starts talking.

“Long ago, there was a terrible famine around here. At that time, a passing Hero recommended growing potatoes. As a result, the people survived the famine and were saved. That’s why potatoes have continued to be loved in this town.”

“Hm… Eating nothing but potatoes isn’t exactly good for your body, though…”

Nutritional balance is important.

By the way, the ration orbs created by the ‘Energy Ball’ spell, which converts mana into nutrients, apparently have perfect nutritional balance. They don’t taste like anything, though…

“Miss, you sure know a lot. The Hero was apparently concerned about that too, and after the famine was over, he warned the townsfolk not to keep eating only potatoes. Also, that Hero had a Blessing that let him control plants, and he could make potatoes grow in no time.”

“How specialized in potatoes was that Hero…?”

Could that Hero really defeat the Demon King by himself?

“Here you go! Six croquettes.”

“Here’s the money. Thanks for the interesting story.”

“Thanks!”

Mio takes the croquettes from the man and returns to us.

“That was a pretty interesting story. I knew it already, but there really are decent Heroes too. It’s just that the Heroes we ran into were especially bad…”

“Of course. If every Hero had a terrible personality, no one would summon them anymore.”

I answer while eating the croquette Mio handed me.

Since otherworld summoning keeps happening, it means that on average, there are more good Heroes.

If only villains could be summoned, no one would want to perform otherworld summoning.

“But even if they’re villains, as long as they can defeat the Demon Race and the Demon King, wouldn’t some people accept it? At worst, they just have to wait out the Hero’s lifespan.”

Sera’s point also makes sense.

Since demons live longer than humans, some might think it’s better to have a Hero defeat the demons, and just endure the Hero’s misdeeds until the Hero’s death.

“It’s an option, but it doesn’t feel very good.”

“Indeed…”

《Tasty!》

Sakura also looks displeased.

Dora, uninterested in the difficult discussion, eats her croquette at her own pace.

By the way, the croquettes Mio bought are quite good, even if they’re not on Mio’s level.

Since this is a potato-producing region, it’s only natural that potato dishes would be good.

“Hm? That statue over there, could it be…?”

Mio points to a bronze statue further down the road.

The statue depicts a boy about our age, wearing a school uniform and holding a potato.

“They’re really thorough…”

“Let’s see… ‘In praise of the achievements of the Hero Jaguar, the Apostle of Potatoes.’”

I read the inscription on the pedestal beneath the statue.

“There are two things to point out. First, why does ‘Apostle of Potatoes’ come before ‘Hero’? Second, what the hell is Jaguar? You look Japanese no matter how you look at it.”

“Jaguar’s probably a fake name. Because he likes potatoes, Jaguar… It’s not very funny, though…”

“And if he liked potatoes that much, it’s possible he prioritized that over being a Hero.”

That’s probably about right, as Mio and Sera say…

“He really was a strange Hero…”

That sums it up.

“I’ve never seen a normal Hero, though.”

“That’s true. Good or bad, Heroes are all strange.”

“I am very sorry.”

Even if Maria apologizes…

Well, she technically is a Hero, but…

I suddenly think of Cynthia, the other locally born Hero. One is a fanatic, the other a battle junkie.

…I see. They don’t really serve as counterexamples to the idea that ‘Heroes are strange.’

This is a complete aside, but there was also an explanation written on the back of the statue.

It described the episode of the town’s founding and said that the Hero decided the town’s name.

The town’s name is Elvalley. If you remove “El”, which indicates a Goddess religion town, you’re left with “Valley”… apparently a play on the word for potato.

And the lord who governs this town apparently wished to be a baron. Since then, the town’s lord has continued to decline opportunities for promotion and remained a baron. Baron Potato, huh?

For the first time in a while, I feel like saying this to a Hero.

You idiot!

---

**AN:** I think it’s about time we can officially call this the Elgant Theocracy arc.

For an Elgant Theocracy arc, surprisingly few people believe it.

+++

## **131: The Dwarf Hero and Foresight**

**AN:** I will say this upfront: in this chapter, Jin does not voluntarily destroy any countries or cities.

That is because Jin is currently in the middle of playing at being a knight. A knight would never destroy a country or city without orders from their lord. And Sakuya would never give such an order.

If this had been free sightseeing, he would have destroyed them.

---

After finishing dinner in the city of Elvalet as the sun went down and the number of people on the streets had thinned, we headed for the final destination of the day.

Leaving the main street, we made our way into a district with a slightly suspicious atmosphere.

“Now that I think about it, it’s been quite a while since I came here.”

The place I was heading for was everyone’s favorite: a slave trader.

“Well, as far as I remember, the last time was when we bought Kate-chan in the Kingdom of Estea?”

“After that, the maids have handled most of the purchases.”

“I was very happy that Jin-sama bought me personally.”

The last time I personally bought a slave from a slave trader was when I bought an apprentice explorer in the Kingdom of Estea.

There were opportunities after that, but if you add the qualifier of ‘from a slave trader’, it still goes back to Estea.

As Sera said, after that it was always the maids who went to slave traders. Slave maids buying new slaves had become little more than a regular event.

By the way, this was after we had sent Sakura and Dora back to the inn.

A slave trader at night is not a place for women and children.

…We will ignore the fact that everyone who remained was a woman or a child. Well, they are all former slaves…

“Since we came to a land without any maids, I figured I’d go myself for once.”

The maids had founded the Advance Trading Company and were expanding its reach.

However, as a rule, they did not enter countries that were not on good terms with me. As a result, they had not touched the Eldia region.

They also avoided places I was certain to visit eventually. This included the Crimson Empire, the elf village, and the demon territory.

The Elgant Theocracy was part of the Eldia region, and since it was already decided that I would head there soon after destroying Eldia, the maids had left it completely untouched.

“If Master is going personally, that means there must be an interesting girl, right? I’m looking forward to it.”

“I’m just following Alta’s recommendation. I’m curious what kind of person she is.”

Mio and I deliberately refrained from checking the map in advance for the sake of fun, so we did not know what kind of slaves were there. We had simply received a report from Alta and decided on a whim to go ourselves.

Maria and Sera had checked in advance since they prioritized my protection over amusement, but they kept quiet so as not to spoil my fun.

Maria’s slightly displeased expression bothered me a little…

After walking for a while, we arrived at the slave trader.

Unlike the high-end slave traders in Estea, this one looked like a normal slave trader and was not very clean.

We went inside, placed the order exactly as Alta had said, and waited for the slaves to be brought out.

“These five are the slaves that match your request.”

The five slaves brought out were seated on a sofa (something that seems to exist everywhere), and I looked them over.

At this point, I lifted the restriction on checking statuses.

Checking them from the right, my eyes stopped on the third girl.

She looked about seven years old, with heavy dark circles under her eyes and messy orange hair that had been left to grow freely. Her expression made it clear that she had given up on everything.

I see…

Name: Rico  

LV2  

Gender: Female  

Age: 15  

Race: Dwarf  

Title: Dwarf Hero  

Skills: \<Seal LV10> \<Inevitable Tragedy LV >

She was the third local Hero, following the beastman Hero and the human Hero.

Are local Heroes always girls?

Because she was a dwarf, she looked about seven, but her actual age was fifteen, not that different from mine.

Putting that aside, what was interesting was that despite being afflicted with \<Seal LV10>, she still possessed what looked like a unique skill.

\<Seal LV10> is granted at the moment a Hero is born. While it is present, all skills at or below the Seal’s level are nullified, and no new skills can be learned.

However, it seemed that skills that did not have a level at birth could not be sealed.

《Jin-sama, the skill she has is a precognition-type skill that I was considering learning myself.》

I received a telepathic message from Maria.

I checked the details of the unique skill.

\<Inevitable Tragedy>  

Allows the user to foresee future crises approaching themselves or those around them. These crises are basically unavoidable. However, if someone with sufficient power becomes involved, that future may be twisted.

《Ah, I see. So Maria had been making that subtle face because someone with the same Hero status had the precognition skill she wanted.》

《!? You noticed!? …Yes, I was a little jealous.》

Being seen through, Maria made an awkward expression.

《This is a precognition skill specialized in crisis avoidance, so I believe it is ideal for protecting Jin-sama. According to Alta, both Jin-sama and I are capable of twisting the future.》

That put us under the category of ‘someone with sufficient power.’

《That is precisely why I believe we must purchase her no matter what.》

《Yeah. In more ways than one, there’s no choice but to buy her.”》

A Hero with a precognition skill. There was no reason not to buy her.

And so, I told the clerk that I would purchase all five slaves here.

“R-really? Buying five will be rather expensive…”

“That’s fine. Clean them up and bring them to me.”

“Y-yes! At once!”

Since these were slaves with troublesome backgrounds who had finally found a buyer, the clerk hurried to prepare them, careful not to miss the opportunity.

In fact, I had requested slaves with ‘dubious backgrounds and unlucky histories’.

This was my own speculation, but I suspected that Rico, a Hero with precognition, had been viewed as creepy by those around her because of her foresight.

Buying the other four at the same time was both to disguise my true purpose and because all of them had fairly rare skills. Also, none of them were marked red (enemy).

Conversely, everyone else here was red-marked, so there was no reason to buy them.

After a while, the five returned, now properly dressed.

I paid the fee for all five and had the \<Slave Art> contracts applied.

During all of this, Rico stared blankly, her mouth slightly open, clearly unable to keep up with what was happening.

“Why…? I was supposed to die without ever being bought…”

Her murmured words, meant for no one to hear, reached my ears clearly.

Leaving the slave trader, we used Portal from the shadows to transfer to Castal’s mansion.

The four other slaves were startled by Portal, but Rico alone remained absentminded, not even noticing that the location had changed.

Leaving the four in the care of the maids, we decided to hear Rico’s story.

“So, when and where were you supposed to die?”

“!? H-how do you know that…? Could it be that you can also see the future…?”

Rico was shocked far beyond normal.

“No. I can’t see the future. I just know that you have the power to foresee death, and that you believe it cannot be overturned.”

Her resigned expression likely came from the fact that her predictions had never once been wrong. No matter how many times she saw her own death, she had never been able to change it.

“Until now… I was never able to change the future…”

“But this time, the future where you die changed, didn’t it?”

“…That is correct. I was supposed to be killed late tonight by bandits who attacked the slave trader. No matter what I did, I would not be bought and would be killed without being able to do anything.”

Now she looked confused as she questioned me.

“Who are you, really? Are you a messenger of the goddess? I hated the goddess who gave me this power, but…”

That’s some useful information.

Although Rico had been in the Elgant Theocracy, she did not seem to worship the goddess.

That saved me the trouble of refuting things. As an aside, Maria had clenched her hand tightly around the ‘messenger of the goddess’ part.

You’re overthinking it…

“I have nothing to do with the goddess. The futures you foresee can be twisted by those with sufficient power. Until now, there simply wasn’t anyone like that around you.”

“Twisted…?”

Rico stared blankly, as if she had been struck by lightning.

“With enough power, you can reject an unwanted future.”

“Enough power…”

At my words, I was certain that a small but fierce flame of fighting spirit had ignited within Rico.

Good. It’s been a while since I used this line.

“Do you want power? Then follow me.”

“Power… I want it… Power to crush unwanted futures…”

She knelt before me, who was deliberately exuding the aura of an evil overlord.

She was already a slave, so obedience was a given, but there was a vast difference in efficiency between forced obedience and voluntary loyalty.

Mio was desperately holding her mouth and stomach to keep from laughing at the ‘do you want power’ line.

Maria and Lucea (who had rushed over when we teleported) nodded in satisfaction when Rico knelt.

“Very well. Then let’s begin by releasing your sealed power.”

Saying that, I held my hand over Rico’s head and retrieved \<Seal>.

Mio was holding back laughter so hard that she had tears in her eyes.

“I can feel power welling up from deep within my body…”

Maria and Cynthia had not felt much change when their Seals were removed, but Rico clearly noticed the difference.

Name: Rico  

LV2  

Gender: Female  

Age: 15  

Race: Dwarf  

Title: Jin’s Slave, Dwarf Hero  

Skills:

Martial  

\<Swordsmanship LV3>

Magic  

\<Light Magic LV3>

Techniques  

\<Appraisal LV1> \<Monster Taming LV1>

Body  

\<Body Enhancement LV2> \<HP Auto Recovery LV2> \<MP Auto Recovery LV2> \<Mind’s Eye LV1> \<Fighting Spirit LV3>

Other  

\<Hero LV3> \<Inevitable Tragedy LV > \<Super Senses LV3>

Hmm? In addition to the basic Hero skill set, there was another unique-looking skill.

\<Super Senses>  

Sharpens the five senses and improves reflexes. Processing ability is also increased, preventing confusion from heightened senses.

I see… Since this one had levels, it must have been sealed.

The fact that she could feel the \<Seal> being removed might also be due to this skill.

…What an incredible find.

Well, I’ve always had a high chance of running into treasures.

After checking her status, we listened to Rico’s past.

She was born in a small village in the Elgant Theocracy and had been treated as creepy from a young age due to \<Inevitable Tragedy>.

Like Maria, she was judged slow to learn because of \<Seal>, which only made the treatment worse.

She was sold into slavery due to her father’s death.

Having lost her mother early, Rico foresaw her father’s death and did everything she could to prevent it, even at the cost of being shunned. In the end, she failed, and rumors spread that she was the cause of his death.

The villagers found her creepy and ultimately chose to sell her to a slave trader.

Rico said she held no grudges against the villagers.

Looking back, she felt that in that situation, it was only natural to be abandoned.

That said, she did not desire reconciliation either. She intended to accept it as the past and live on.

“I am the one at fault for lacking the power to change the future. I must become strong…”

After finishing her story, Rico murmured those words with eyes full of resolve.

The flame of fighting spirit within her was clearly stronger than before.

After hearing her out, we explained our own situation.

…Or rather, we planned to leave the details to the maids.

After all, this period would be used for Rico’s education.

After some training, we planned to have Rico accompany us on our journey.

As with Cynthia, local Heroes tended to be quite eccentric, so I wanted to observe her for a while.

Since Rico had abilities well-suited for guarding, she might make a good exclusive guard for Sakuya. Though, Tamo-san was already guarding Sakuya.

Because a dwarf’s age was hard to judge by appearance, if she wore a maid outfit, she could pass as a maid of appropriate age.

So we limited ourselves to a rough explanation of abilities and Rico’s role going forward.

“I am a Hero of this world…? If I’m a Hero, can I become strong?”

“Yeah. As far as I know, you can become quite strong by this world’s standards.”

“In that case, I don’t mind.”

She did not ask for specifics, only whether it led directly to strength.

Cynthia was a battle maniac against monsters, and I sensed something similar from Rico.

“If I can become strong, I’ll endure any training. I don’t want to lose to a hopeless future.”

It seemed the firewood I had thrown onto her fighting spirit burned far more fiercely than I had expected. Very good.

Leaving Rico with Lucea, we returned to the inn in Elvalet.

Since Rico would be accompanying us as a maid in name, maid training would be done in parallel.

Rico wanted to skip maid training and focus on combat training, but she was intimidated into silence by Lucea.

Lucea would never allow someone lacking discipline or education to accompany me.

We explained the events to Sakura and Dora, who had stayed behind.

“So, that means a Hero with precognition has joined us.”

“Precognition… That’s an amazing skill…”

Sakura seemed surprised by the sudden appearance of such an extraordinary ability.

“Yeah. It seems she can only predict crises to herself and those around her, but that’s more than enough. If you have the power to avoid those predictions, it’s perfect.”

《Amazing!》

Dora probably did not really understand.

“That aside, Master, you looked like you were really into it when you made Rico swear loyalty.”

Mio grinned as she looked at me.

Yes. I was fully into it.

“Mio-chan, the first impression is the most important. That exchange engraved into Ricos soul that Jin-sama is worthy of her loyalty. It was good to see something like that again.”

“…”

Even Mio could not comment on Maria’s satisfied declaration.

When someone who was almost a believer from the start said that, it carried weight.

For the record, Rico had not become a believer yet. The reason was that the color of her eyes at the end had been slightly concerning.

“Anyway, Rico will become strong. Her goal and aptitude align perfectly.”

She wished to become strong enough to crush fate, and she possessed the abilities to do so. There was no way she would not become strong.

Like the golden fox Tokoyo, she might become one of the future strongest candidates.

The next morning, when I got out of bed and opened the window, I saw smoke rising from the direction of the slave trader we had visited.

Checking the map, it was indeed the remains of that slave trader, burned down.

As Rico had said, bandits must have snuck in during the night and set it on fire.

There were no survivors.

The perpetrators had already been caught, and investigations and interrogations would begin.

“Haha… So this is the result of Rico’s foresight. That’s pretty powerful.”

If I had not bought her, Rico would have been killed by the bandits.

Just barely safe…

I was likely the last customer of that slave trader.

To avoid unnecessary trouble, we decided to leave Elvalet promptly. The ministers had recovered after a day of rest.

Eljaguar… no, Elvalley. A week had passed since we left.

Judging by the map, we should be nearing the divine capital. Of course, I meant via my Special Power.

Since we were taking a wide detour to avoid the city where the scouts had caused trouble, it would still take about three more days by carriage.

Incidentally, during this week, we stopped by several cities, but our identities were never exposed.

Every city had slave traders, but none were as interesting as Elvalet, so we left purchases to the maids.

They had extensive experience with slave purchases, after all (over 5000 people).

“In the end, we cut through the forest to shorten the route, only to waste time taking detours. Kind of pointless.”

“Sorry. I didn’t think the Elgant Theocracy would show such clear hostility… no, killing intent. I thought they would restrain themselves with common sense, even if they felt disgust.”

Sakuya looked apologetic, as the response from the Holy Kingdom had been beyond her expectations.

Sakura offered comfort.

“You didn’t do anything wrong, Sakuya-chan… right?”

“Thank you, Sakura-chan. But I did underestimate them…”

Encouraged by Sakura’s words, Sakuya showed a small smile.

“If this was going to happen, maybe we should have used inferior wind dragons to fly straight there, or secretly placed Portals and moved the ministers all at once.”

“That would have caused all kinds of trouble…”

Using inferior wind dragons would certainly violate airspace and cause problems.

But still…

“Trouble would have happened even without them, wouldn’t it?”

“…When you put it that way, you’re right.”

We were already in plenty of trouble.

“When the summit was first proposed, you said that cutting through other countries airspace with an elite knight order would be problematic, but that was strange to begin with.”

“What do you mean?”

“They’re the ones who invited us. You could have taken a stronger stance, like saying they have no right to complain about our means of travel.”

“I’m not you, Brother. I can’t be that aggressive…”

Sakuya gave a wry smile.

Personally, I thought showing strength before negotiations to assert one’s position was a valid approach.

But I had left the negotiations to Sakuya, so I should not interfere too much.

“As long as you won’t be weak during the summit, that’s fine.”

“Don’t worry. Leave it to me. I have absolutely no intention of accepting any terms that would put you or Castal at a disadvantage.”

“Yeah, I’ll leave it to you. No matter what you say, we’ll back you up, so don’t worry.”

“I’m counting on you for that too.”

Put simply, she would be making strong statements in enemy territory. There was no guarantee her safety would not be at risk.

Since I was leaving the negotiations to Sakuya, ensuring her personal safety was our responsibility.

As we were talking, the area changed, and the divine capital of the Elgant Theocracy became visible on the map.

This time, since we were acting as guards, we checked without hesitation for high-level individuals and those with special skills.

“Pfuh!?”

“Eh!? What’s wrong, Master!?”

Seeing me burst out laughing, Mio let out a strange cry.

“Oh! The map… But what did you see…?”

“I searched for dangerous individuals.”

Understanding immediately but not knowing the specifics, Mio prompted me to explain.

“I see. Let’s take a look…”

Not just Mio, but the others did the same search.

“There are… a lot of them…”

《So many amazing ones!》

“Indeed. Troublesome skills. Unnatural titles. Blessings. Unique skill holders. I did not expect this many.”

“We must raise the alert level to protect Jin-sama.”

As everyone said, there were far too many dangerous and high-risk individuals staying in the divine capital, Elgare.

They included common citizens, nobles attending the summit, and even the leadership of the Holy Kingdom itself.

If I introduced them all, it would take all day.

“For now, lets pick out those most likely to be hostile.”

“I believe the king of the Kingdom of Glantz has a high likelihood of hostility. There was also a carriage attack plan in the Kingdom of Sanokia.”

Maria pointed out Zenon, the king of the Kingdom of Glantz, who was likely attending the summit.

He was dangerous in every sense, especially his race.

Name: Zenon Glantz  

LV169  

Gender: Male  

Age: 9  

Race: Human (Possessed)  

Skills:

Martial  

\<Swordsmanship LV10> \<Spear Technique LV10> \<Archery LV10> \<Shield Technique LV10> \<Unarmed Combat LV10> \<Mounted Combat LV10>

Techniques  

\<Command LV10> \<Inspiration LV10> \<Horsemanship LV10>

Body  

\<Body Enhancement LV10> \<Jumping LV10> \<Search LV10> \<HP Auto Recovery LV10> \<MP Auto Recovery LV10> \<Presence Detection LV10> \<Poison Resistance LV10>

Curses  

\<Existence Possession LV > \<Crawling Bloodstain LV >

Titles: King of the Kingdom of Glantz, First King of the Kingdom of Glantz

Zenon’s race is Human. However, it has “Possessed” appended to it.

His age being nine. His level and skill levels being abnormally high. The contradictory titles of “King of the Kingdom of Glantz” and “First King of the Kingdom of Glantz.” …And finally, the curse mark he somehow possesses: \<Existence Possession>.

\<Existence Possession>  

Allows possession of the body of someone with a similar soul form. Control of the body goes to the one with the stronger will.

In other words, Zenon Glantz… or rather, the unnamed first king of Glantz had likely survived by possessing his descendants generation after generation.

Levels and skills seemed tied to the soul rather than the body, carrying over after possession.

“Just from what we can see, it’s clear he’s done all sorts of things.”

“Yeah. He definitely doesn’t have normal sensibilities. I can see why he’d be hostile…”

Mio and I nodded.

He did not look like someone who had lived a normal life.

Earlier, we had speculated that demons were behind a nine-year-old ascending the throne of Glantz, but that now seemed less likely.

Since he could possess bodies himself, transferring the throne would be easy.

Conversely, the existence of \<Existence Possession>, a curse mark befitting a Four Heavenly Kings-type enemy, raised the possibility that demons had been active for far longer.

“He will likely attend the summit, so avoiding involvement is impossible.”

“He’s royalty, but not a woman, so he doesn’t hit your weak spot, Brother.”

“Sakuya, could you stop making it sound like I’d recruit any female royal… If he’s as we suspect, I wouldn’t take him as a subordinate regardless of gender.”

“Really?”

Sakuya’s perception of me was terrible.

I admitted that many female royals were my subordinates, but character was always a condition.

Like Christia, the former Eldia princess, there were cases where I did not recruit them despite the opportunity.

“Of course. I have no intention of recruiting someone who went too far.”

“Right. You only treat decent people decently.”

“Exactly.”

If someone was already beyond the line by my standards, I would never recruit them. Slavery for silencing aside.

“Low chance, but if Zenon turns out to be decent and has no intention of opposing us, fine. But if he clearly and directly opposes us, I’ll crush him without mercy.”

“Please don’t go too far…”

Sakuya said with half-resignation.

“Even if his stats are high, we surpass them. I doubt we would lose in a straight fight. But he’s lived a long time. We don’t know what tricks he might use, so let’s not let our guard down.”

“This time, the ministers are with us, so it may not go as before.”

As Sera said, the ministers were not subordinates.

Protecting them while dealing with troublesome enemies could be difficult.

“That’s why, for the summit, I plan to bring the highest-level elite maid knights as guards. I’ve already informed Lucea.”

“As expected of Master. Very thorough.”

Even among the maid knights, there were differences in strength.

For the summit, I wanted the strongest ones to ensure the ministers’ safety.

…The summit was completely being treated as enemy territory.

**AN:** The Third Hero Appears. Once again, loli. Well, she’s fifteen inside, so loli classification is debatable?

This is for later, but I’m planning to make the elf Hero (if one appears) fairly old.

Also, I partially changed the merfolk settings.

1. Changed ‘physical maturity is fast’ to ‘only royalty matures quickly.’

2. Changed \<Enthralling Song> from a no-level skill to a level-based skill.

3. The first keeps open the possibility of loli merfolk. The second creates differentiation among merfolk through racial skills, similar to dragonkin \<Dragon Magic>.
